RatioOfTheDecision	Whilst c onsidering such a submission one must keep in mind that the desire to establish educational or other institutions for the benefit of students of their own community would be there not only in minority communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such a desire would be there in all citizens and communities, whether majority or minority.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the majority communities, whether religious or linguistic, can establish and administer educational institutions for their own community at their own costs why should the position be different for minorities.
RatioOfTheDecision	If an educational institute established by a majority community for members of that community only, takes <ORG> aid, it would then lose the right to admit only students of its own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	it would have to comply with the Constitutional mandate of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	The position is no different for an educational institute established by a minority.
RatioOfTheDecision	The basic feature of our Constitution is equality and secularism.
RatioOfTheDecision	It follows that the minority cannot be a more privileged class or section of citizen.
RatioOfTheDecision	At  the cost of repetition it is again emphasised that Article 30 does not deal with minorities who are economically or socially backward.
RatioOfTheDecision	These are not communities whose children are not capable of competing on merit, e.g.
RatioOfTheDecision	a Tamilian in Tamil competes with others and gets admission on merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even when he/she shifts to Maharashtra he/she continues to be able to compete openly and get admission on merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	Merely because a Tamilian shifts to Maharashtra or some other State does not mean that Tamilian becomes a citizen entitled to special privilege or rights not available to other citizens.
RatioOfTheDecision	This was not the purpose or object of Article 30.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 30 was framed only to ensure that the Maharashtrians, by reason of their being politically powerful, do not prevent the Tamilian from establishing an educational institution at their own cost.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 20 merely protects the right of the minority to establish and administer an educational institution, i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	to have the same rights as those enjoyed by majority.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 30 giv es no right to receive <ORG> aid.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is for the institution to decide whether it wants to received aid.
RatioOfTheDecision	If it decides to take <ORG> aid then Article 30(2) merely provides that the <ORG> will not discriminate against it.
RatioOfTheDecision	When <ORG>, whilst giving aid, asks the minority educational institute to comply with a constitutional mandate, it can hardly be said that the <ORG> is discriminating against that institute.
RatioOfTheDecision	The <ORG> is bound to ensure that all educational institutes, whether majority or minority, comply with the constitutional mandate.
RatioOfTheDecision	37.
RatioOfTheDecision	Another respect to be kept in mind is that in practical terms, throwing open admission to all, does not affect rights under Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	If the educational institution is for purposes of teaching the religion or language of the concerned minority, then even though admission is thrown open to all very few students of other communities will take admission in such an educational institution.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the educational institution is giving general secular education, then the minor ity character of that institution does not get affected by having a majority of students from other communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even though the majority of students may be from other communities the institution will still be under the management of the minority.
RatioOfTheDecision	Further if the educational institution is a school, then the management will, in spite of Article 29(2 ), still be able to take a sizable number of students from their own community into the school.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 29(2) precludes reservations on grounds of religion, race, caste or language.
RatioOfTheDecision	But it does not preclude giving of preference, if everything else is equal.
RatioOfTheDecision	Admission into schools generally are by interview.
RatioOfTheDecision	At this stage there is no common entrance test which determines merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	Undoubtedly children of the minority communities, contemplated by Article 30(1 ), would be as bright or capable as children of other communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus whilst admitting at this stage preference can always be given to members of their own community so long as some students of other communities  are also admitted and denial is not on basis of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus for admissions in schools, Article 29(2) will pose no difficulty to minority institutions.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, Article 29(2) will require, if <ORG> aid is taken, that admissions into college, either under graduate or post graduate and admission into professional course, be not denied to any citizen on grounds of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	This would mean that admissions must be on merit from the common entrance test prescribed by the <ORG> or <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Here also if two students have equal merit, preference can be given to a student of their own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	Also Article 29(2) does not preclude minority (or even other educational institutions) admitting or denying admission on grounds other than religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus e.g.
RatioOfTheDecision	preferential admission could be given to those students who are willing to serve the community or work in a particular region, for a particular period  of time after passing out.
RatioOfTheDecision	Also in such cases marks not exceeding 15% can be allotted for interviews.
RatioOfTheDecision	This will ensure that a sufficient number of students of their own community are admitted.
RatioOfTheDecision	More importantly there is no reason to believe that students of these minority communities will not be able to compete on merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	A sizable number will be available on merit also.
RatioOfTheDecision	38.
RatioOfTheDecision	Most importantly we are interpreting the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	As the language of Articles 29(2) and 30 is clear and unambiguous the <ORG> has to give effect to it, irrespective of the consequences.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is all the more necessary as the same is in consonance with the intention of the framers.
RatioOfTheDecision	<ORG> cannot give an interpretation which creates a clash where none exits.
RatioOfTheDecision	<ORG> cannot add words which the framers purposely omitted to use/add.
RatioOfTheDecision	<ORG>s cannot give an interpretation, not supported by a plain reading, on considerations, such as minority educational institutions not being able to admit their own students.
RatioOfTheDecision	To be remembered that there is no com pulsion to receive <ORG> aid.
Precedent	As was mentioned during the Constituent Assembly Debates the management can refuse to take aid.
Precedent	But if they choose to take <ORG> aid, then even a minority educational institution must abide by the Constitutional mandate of Article 29(2) just as they have to comply with the Constitutional mandate of Article 28(2) and comply with general secular laws of the country.
Precedent	39.
Precedent	Thus looked at either from the historical point of view and/or the intention of the framers and/or from the contextual viewpoint and/or from principles of interpretation it is clear that Article 29(2) fully applies to Article 30.
Precedent	If a minority educational institute chooses to take <ORG> aid, it cannot then refuse to admit students on grounds of religion, race, case, language or any of them.
Precedent	40.
Precedent	Now let us see whether the principles of "stare decisis" require us to take a different view.
Precedent	A large number of authorities have been cited and one has to consider these authorities.
Precedent	41.
Precedent	The first case, which was decided a s far back as on 9th April, 1951, was the case of <CITATION_149321> .
Precedent	It is reported in (1951) SCR 525.
Precedent	In this case the <ORG> of Madras was maintaining <ORG>.
Precedent	In those colleges, for many years before the commencement of the Constitution, the seats used to be filled up in a proportion, set forth in what was called "the Communal G.O.".
Precedent	The allocation of seats was as follows:     Anglo-Indians and Indian Muslims 1"  After the Constitution was framed a Writ Petition under Article 226 came to be filed by <NAME> and one another in <ORG>.
Argument	She complained that this Communal G. O. affected her fundamental rights, inter alia, under Article 29(2).
Argument	On behalf of the <ORG> it was argued that there was no discrimination and no infringement of fundamental rights.
Argument	It was argued that it was the duty of the <ORG> to take care of and promote educational and economic interest of the weaker section of the people.
Argument	It was argued that giving preferences and/or reser vations did not violate Article 29(2).
Precedent	This argument was repelled and it was held as follows:  "It will be noticed that while Clause (1) protects the language, script or culture of a section of the citizens, Clause (2) guarantees the fundamental right of an individual citizen.
Precedent	The right to get admission into any educational institution of the kind mentioned in Clause (2) is a right which an individual citizen has as a citizen and not as a member of any community or class of citizens.
Precedent	This right is not to be denied to the citizen on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	If a citizen who seeks admission into any such educational institution has not the requisite academic qualifications and is denied admission on that ground, he certainly cannot be heard to complain of an infraction of his fundamental right under this article.
RatioOfTheDecision	But, on the other hand, if he has the academic qualifications but is refused admission only on ground of religion, race, caste, language or any of them, then ther e is a clear breach of his fundamental rights.
RatioOfTheDecision	xxx xxx xxx xxx xxx xxx  Take the case of the petitioner <NAME>.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is not disputed that he secured a much larger number of marks than the marks secured by many of the Non-Brahmin candidates and yet the Non-Brahmin candidates who secured less number of marks will be admitted into six out of every 14 seats but the petitioner <NAME> will not be admitted into any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	What is the reason for this denial of admission except that he is a Brahmin and not a Non-Brahmin.
RatioOfTheDecision	He may have secured higher marks than the Anglo-Indian and Indian Christians or Muslim candidates but nevertheless, he cannot get any of the seats reserved for the last mentioned communities for no fault of his except that he is a Brahmin and not a member of the aforesaid communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Such denial of admission cannot but be regarded as made on ground only of his caste.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is argued that the petitioners are not denied admission only because they are Brahmins but for a variety of reasons, e.g.,  (a) they are Brahmins, (b) Brahmins have an allotment of only two seats out of 14 and  (c) the two seats have already been filled up by more meritorious Brahmin candidates.
RatioOfTheDecision	This may be true so far as these two seats reserved for the Brahmin are concerned but this line of argument can have no force when we come to consider the seats reserved for candidates of other communities, for so far as those seats are concerned, the petitioners are denied admission into any of them not on any ground other than the sole ground of their being Brahmins and not being members of the community for whom these reservations have been made.
RatioOfTheDecision	The classification in <ORG> proceeds on the basis of the religion, race and caste.
RatioOfTheDecision	In our view, the classification made in <ORG> is opposed to the Constitution and constitutes a clear violation of the fundamental rights guaranteed to the citizen under Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	In this view of the matter, we do not find it necessary to consider the effect of Articles 14 or 15 on th e specific articles discussed above."
Precedent	Thus as far back as in 1951 it has been held that Article 29(2) does not permit reservation in favour of any caste, community or class of people.
Precedent	An argument based on the word "only" in Article 29(2 ), to the effect that admitting students of their own community did not amount to refusing admission on grounds of religion, race, caste, language or any of them was rejected.
Precedent	Undoubtedly, this was a case pertaining to educational institutions maintained by the <ORG>.
Precedent	But the interpretation of Article 29(2) would remain the same even in respect of "educational institutions aided by the <ORG>".
Precedent	In all such institutions there can be no reservations based on religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	The term "any educational Institution" in Article 29(2) would also include a minority educational institution under Article 30.
Precedent	Thus the interpretation of Article 29(2) would remain the same even in respect of a minority educational institution under Article 30(1).
Precedent	42.
Precedent	In Cha <NAME> case the reservations were not just for economically or socially backward communities.
Precedent	There were reservations for Anglo Indians, Indian Christians, Muslims, Brahmins and Non-Brahmins.
Precedent	After this Court struck down the reservation the framers of the Constitution amended Article 15 by adding Article 15(4) which reads as follows: "15(4).
Precedent	Nothing in this article or in Clause (2) of Article 29 shall prevent the <ORG> from making any special provision for the advancement of any socially and educationally backward classes of citizens or for the Scheduled Castes and the Scheduled Tribes."
Precedent	Thus when the framers of the Constitution did not want Article 29(2) to apply they have specially so provided.
Precedent	Significantly no such amendment was made in Article 30(1) even though reservations in favour of minority communities was also held to be violative of Article 29(2).
Precedent	43.
Precedent	In the case of the <CITATION_1964375> .
Precedent	reported in  an Anglo-Indian School, called <ORG> at Deolali, received aid from t he <ORG> of Bombay.
Precedent	The <ORG> of Bombay issued a circular order on 6th January, 1954 which enjoined that no primary or secondary school could admit to a class where English is used as the medium of instruction, any pupil other than the pupil whose mother tongue was English.
Precedent	This was challenged in a Writ Petition under Article 226 in <ORG>.
Precedent	The Petition having been allowed, the <ORG> filed an Appeal to this Court.
Precedent	This Court held as follows: "Assuming, however, that under the impugned order a section of citizens, other than Anglo-Indian and citizens of non-Asiatic descent, whose language is English, may also get admission, even then citizens, whose language is not English, are certainly debarred by the order from admission to a School where English is used as a medium of instruction in all the classes.
Precedent	Article 29(2) ex facie puts no limitation or qualification on the expression "citizen".
RatioOfTheDecision	Therefore, the construction sought to be put upon Clause 5 does not apparently help the learned Attorney -General, for even on that construction the order will contravene the provisions of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	The learned Attorney-General then falls back upon two contentions to avoid the applicability of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	In the first place he contends that Article 29(2) does not confer any fundamental right on all citizens generally but guarantees the rights of citizens of minority groups by providing that they must not be denied admission to educational institutions maintained by the <ORG> or receiving aid out of the <ORG> funds on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them and he refers us to the marginal note to the article.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is certainly a new contention put forward before us for the first time.
RatioOfTheDecision	It does not appear to have been specifically taken in the affidavits in opposition filed in <ORG> and there is not indication in the judgment under appeal that it was advanced in this form before <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Nor was this point specifically made a ground of appeal in the petition for lea ve to appeal to this Court.
RatioOfTheDecision	Apart from this, the contention appears to us to be devoid of merit.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 29(1) gives protection to any section of the citizens having a distinct language, script or culture by guaranteeing their right to conserve the same.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 30(1) secures to all minorities, whether based on religion or language, the right to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice.
RatioOfTheDecision	Now suppose the <ORG> maintains an educational institution to help conserving the distinct language, script or culture of a section of the citizens or makes grants in aid to an educational institution established by a minority community based on religion or language to conserve their distinct language, script or culture, who can claim the protection of Article 29(2) in the matter of admission into any such institution?
RatioOfTheDecision	Surely the citizens of the very section whose language, script or culture is sought to be conserved by the institution or the citizens who belong to the very minority group which has est ablished and is administering the institution, do not need any protection against themselves and therefore Article 29(2) is not designed for the protection of this section or this minority.
RatioOfTheDecision	Nor do we see any reason to limit Article 29(2) to citizens belonging to a minority group other than the section or the minorities referred to in Article 29(1) or Article 30(1 ), for the citizens, who do no belong to any minority group, may quite conceivably need this protection just as much as the citizens of such other minority groups.
RatioOfTheDecision	If it is urged that the citizens of the majority group are amply protected by Article 15 and do not require the protection of Article 29(2 ), then there are several obvious answers to that argument.
Precedent	The language of Article 29(2) is wide and unqualified and may well cover all citizens whether they belong to the majority or minority group.
Precedent	Article 15 protects all citizens against the <ORG> whereas the protection of Article 29(2) extends against the <ORG> or any body who denies the right conf erred by it.
Precedent	Further Article 15 protects all citizens against discrimination generally but Article 29(2) is a protection against a particular species of wrong namely denial of admission into educational institutions of the specified kind.
Precedent	In the next place Article 15 (SIC) quite general and wide in its terms and applies to all citizens, whether they belong to the majority or minority groups, and gives protection to all the citizens against discrimination by the <ORG> on certain specific grounds.
Precedent	Article 29(2) confers a special right on citizens for admission into educational institutions maintained or aided by the <ORG>.
Precedent	To limit this right only to citizens belonging to minority groups will be to provide a double protection for such citizens and to hold that the citizens of the majority group have no special educational rights in the nature of a right to be admitted into an educational institution for the maintenance of which they make contributions by way of taxes.
RatioOfTheDecision	We see no cogent reason for such discrimina tion.
RatioOfTheDecision	The heading under which articles 29 and 30 are grouped together -- namely "Cultural and Educational Rights" -- is quite general and does not in terms contemplate such differentiation.
RatioOfTheDecision	If the fact that the institution is maintained or aided out of <ORG> funds is the basis of this guaranteed right then all citizens, Irrespective of whether they belong to the majority or minority groups, are alike entitled to the protection of this fundamental right.
RatioOfTheDecision	In view of all these considerations the marginal note alone, on which the Attorney-General relies, cannot be read as controlling the plain meaning of the language in which Article 29(2) has been couched.
Precedent	Indeed in <CITATION_149321> [(1951) SCR 525], this <ORG> has already held as follows: "It will be noticed that while Clause (1) protects the language, script or culture or a section of the citizens, Clause (2) guarantees the fundamental right of an individual citizen.
Precedent	The right to get admission into any educational institution of the kind mentioned in Clause ( 2) is a right which an individual citizen has as a citizen and not as a member of any community or class of citizens."
Precedent	In our judgment this part of the contention of the learned Attorney-General cannot be sustained."
Precedent	(emphasis supplied) In this case it was also argued that the word "only" in Article 29(2) had to be given some meaning and that the circular order did not deny citizens admission only on ground of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	It was submitted that the object of the circular order was to secure advancement of Hindi which was ultimately to be the National language.
Precedent	It was submitted that thus there was no denial "only" on the ground of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	It was submitted that the denial was for the purposes of promoting the advancement of the national language and to facilitate imparting of education through the medium of the pupils mother tongue.
Precedent	this argument was repelled in the following terms: "Granting that the object of the impugned order before  us was what is claimed for it by the learned Attorney-General, the question still remains as to how that object has been sought to be achieved.
RatioOfTheDecision	Obviously that is sought to be done by denying to all pupils, whose mother tongue is not English, admission into any School where the medium of instruction is English.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whatever the object, the immediate ground and direct cause for the denial is that the mother tongue of the pupil is not English.
RatioOfTheDecision	Adapting the language of Lord <NAME>, it may be said that the laudable object of the impugned order does not obviate the prohibition of Article 29(2) because the effect of the order involved an infringement of this fundamental right, and that effect is brought about by denying admission only on the ground of language.
RatioOfTheDecision	The same principle is implicit in the decision of this <ORG> in <CITATION_149321> [(1951) SCR 525].
RatioOfTheDecision	There also the object of the impugned communal G.O.
RatioOfTheDecision	was to advance the interest of educationally backward classes of citizens but, that object notwithstanding , this <ORG> struck down the order as unconstitutional because the modus operandi to achieve that object was directly based only on one of the forbidden grounds specified in the article.
Precedent	In our opinion the impugned order offends against the fundamental right guaranteed to all citizens by Article 29(2)."
Precedent	It may be mentioned, even though not relevant for the purposes of this judgment, that in this case it has also been submitted that the rights under Article 30(1) are only for the purposes of conserving language, script or culture as set out in Article 29(1).
Precedent	This argument was also repelled by this <ORG>.
Precedent	44.
Precedent	Thus, as far back in 1955, <ORG> of this <ORG> has held that Article 29(2) is applicable to Article 30.
Precedent	It has been held that even in a minority educational institution all citizens of India are entitled to admission.
Precedent	It has been held that a citizen cannot be denied admission in a minority educational institution on ground "only" of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	To be no ted that one of the petitions was from the Gujarati Hindu community and she was seeking admission into an Anglo-Indian School.
Precedent	Her right to be admitted was upheld.
Precedent	It has been categorically held that Article 29(2) applied to an Article 30 educational institute.
Precedent	The framers of the Constitution did not and have not amended the Constitution to provide otherwise.
Precedent	45.
Argument	In Re The Kerala Education Bill, 1957 reported in (1959) SCR 995, the President of India made a Reference under Article 143(1) of the Constitution of India for obtaining opinion of this Court upon certain questions relating to the constitutional validity of some of the provisions of the Kerala Education Bill which had been passed by <ORG>, but had been reserved by the Governor for consideration of the President of India.
Argument	The questions which were referred to this Court for consideration were as follows:  "(1) Does Sub-clause (5) of Clause 3 of the Kerala Education Bill, read with Clause 36 thereof, or any of the provisions o f the said sub-clause, offend Article 14 of the Constitution in any particulars or to any extent?
Argument	(2) Do Sub-clause (5) of Clause 3, Sub-clause (3) of Clause 8 and Clauses 9 to 13 of Kerala Education Bill, or any provision thereof, offend Clause (1) of Article 30 of the Constitution in any particulars or to any extent.
Precedent	(3) Does Clause 15 of the Kerala Education Bill, or any provisions thereof, offend Article 14 of the Constitution in any particulars or to any extent?
Precedent	(4) Does Clause 33 of the Kerala Education Bill, or any provisions thereof, offend Article 226 of the Constitution in any particulars or to any extent?"
Precedent	46.
RatioOfTheDecision	Only question No.2 is relevant for our purposes.
RatioOfTheDecision	Whilst answering question No.2 this <ORG>, inter alia, observed as follows: "Re.
RatioOfTheDecision	Question 2: Articles 29 and 30 are set out in Part III of our Constitution which guarantees our fundamental rights.
RatioOfTheDecision	They are grouped together under the sub-head "Cultural and Educational Rights".
RatioOfTheDecision	The text and the marginal notes of both the Articles show that their  purpose is to confer those fundamental rights on certain sections of the community which constitute minority communities.
Precedent	Under Clause (1) Article 29 and section of the citizens residing in the territory of India or any part thereof having a distinct language, script or culture of its own has the right to conserve the same.
Precedent	It is obvious that a minority community can effectively conserve its language, script or culture by and though educational institutions and, therefore, the right to establish and maintain educational institutions of its choice is a necessary concomitant to the right to conserve its distinctive language, script or culture and that is what is conferred on all minorities by Article 30(1) which has hereinbefore been quoted in full.
Precedent	This right, however, is subject to Clause 2 of Article 29 which provides that no citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution maintained by the <ORG> or receiving aid out of <ORG> funds on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any  of them.
Precedent	xxx xxx xxx xxx xxx xxx  The second proviso imposes the condition that at least 40 per cent of the annual admissions must be made available to the members of communities other than the Anglo- Indian community.
Precedent	Likewise Article 29(2) provides, inter alia, that no citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution receiving aid out of <ORG> funds on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
Precedent	These are the only constitutional limitations to the right of the Anglo-Indian educational institutions to receive aid.
Precedent	Learned counsel appearing for two Anglo-Indian schools contends that the <ORG> of Kerala is bound to implement the provisions of Article 337.
Precedent	Indeed it is stated in the statement of case filed by the <ORG> of Kerala that all Christian schools are aided by that <ORG> and, therefore, the Anglo-Indian schools, being also Chiristian schools, have been so far getting from the <ORG> of Kerala the grant that they are entitled to under Article 337.
Precedent	Their grievance is  that by introducing this Bill the <ORG> of Kerala is now seeking to impose besides the constitutional limitations mentioned in the second proviso to Article 337 and Article 29(2 ), further and more onerous conditions on this grant to the Anglo-Indian educational institutions although their constitutional right to such grant still subsist."
Precedent	(emphasis supplied)  47.
Precedent	In this case it was argued on behalf of the <ORG> that as the minority instate received <ORG> aid it was bound, by virtue of Article 29(2 ), to admit students of all communities and thus did not retain its minority character.
Precedent	That Article 29(2) applied to a minority educational institute was not denied.
Precedent	The argument that, it lost its minority character because it admitted students of other communities, was repelled in the following terms.
Precedent	"By admitting a non-member into it the minority institution does not shed its character and cease to be a minority institution.
Precedent	Indeed the object of conservation of the distinct language, script and culture of a  minority may be better served by propagating the same amongst non- members of the particular minority community.
Precedent	In our opinion, it is not possible to read this condition into Article 30(1) of the Constitution."
Precedent	Thus even in this case it has been accepted and held that Article 26(2) applies to minority educational institutions established under Article 30.
Precedent	It has been held that merely because students of other communities are admitted, the institute does not lose its minority character.
Precedent	In this case it was also held that <ORG> can prescribe reasonable regulations.
Precedent	In this case regulations which provided for qualifications of teachers and which provided for <ORG> Public Service Commission to select teachers in aide schools were upheld.
Precedent	Thus even in this case it is accepted that Article 29(2) would govern Article 30(1).
Precedent	48.
Precedent	<CITATION_751632> , the petitioners belonged to <ORG>.
Precedent	They maintained educational institutions primarily for the benefit of the Christian community.
Precedent	Admitted ly these institutions did not receive <ORG> aid.
Precedent	Therefore, the question of Article 29(2) and its applicability to Article 30 did not arise.
Precedent	On the contrary (as is set out on page 840 of the Report) it was an admitted position that these institutions did not deny admissions to students belonging to other communities.
Precedent	<ORG> issued an order directing all private training colleges to reserve 60% of the seats for trainee teachers of the schools maintained by the Board.
Precedent	It was held that this Order violated rights under Article 30.
Precedent	All observations made in this case are in this context.
Precedent	They cannot be drawn out of context to hold that even where a minority institute receives aid the Constitutional mandate of Article 29(2) would not apply.
Precedent	In this case also it is held that the rights under Article 30(1) are subject to reasonable restrictions and regulations.
Precedent	It was held that restrictions in the interest of efficiency, discipline, health, sanitation, public order etc.
Precedent	could be imposed.
Precedent	49.
RatioOfTheDecision	<CITATI ON_833521> , the petitioners maintained <ORG> which was affiliate to <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	With effect form 1st March, 1962 Section 48-A was introduced.
RatioOfTheDecision	Under this Section <ORG> was established for affiliated colleges.
RatioOfTheDecision	Sub-clause (e) of Section 48-A provided that appointments, dismissals, removals, termination of service or deduction in rank teachers of an affiliated college should be made by the Governing body of the college on the recommendation of the <ORG>.
Fact	Further, Sub-clause (11) provided that all disciplinary actions could be taken only in consultation with the <ORG>.
Fact	The petitioners challenged the virus of the provision and claimed that it affected their rights under Article 30(1) of the Constitution.
Fact	Whilst the Petition was pending in this Court; Section 48-B was introduced in the Bihar State Universities Act, which provided that appointments, dismissals, removals, termination of service or reduction in rank of teachers or disciplinary measures could  only be taken with the approval of the <ORG> and the <ORG> of the University.
Fact	This was also challenged.
Fact	Thus in this case the interplay of Sections 29(2) and 30(1) did not come into questions at all.
Fact	In this case it was an admitted position that the college was open to non-Catholics also.
Precedent	One of the arguments raised on behalf of the <ORG> was that since the admissions were not reserved only for students of the <ORG> community the college did not qualify for protection under Article 30(1).
Precedent	This argument was negatived by holding that merely because members of other communities were admitted to the institution did not mean the institution lost its minority character.
Precedent	This case thus shows that even if members of other community are admitted into the institution the institution would still remain a minority institution which is under the management of the minority.
Precedent	50.
Precedent	<CITATION_1649950> , an educational institute was started by a Christian with the help of funds received from <ORG> y.
Precedent	The question was whether the institute was not entitled to protection of Article 30(1) merely because funds were obtained from United Kingdom and the management was carried on by some persons who may not have been born in India.
Precedent	This Court held that rights under Article 29 could only be claimed by Indian citizens, but Article 30 guarantees the rights of minority.
Precedent	It was held that the said Article does not refer to citizenship as the qualification for members of the minority.
Precedent	This case therefore does not deal with the question of the interplay between Articles 29(2) and 30(1).
Precedent	51.
Precedent	In the case of <CITATION_686466> reported in (1971) 1 SCR 734, the Constitutional validity of Sections 48, 49, 53, 56, 58 and 63 of the Kerala University Act was challenged as violation the rights under Section 30(1) .
Precedent	In this case there is no discussion regarding the effect of Article 29(2) on Article 30.
Precedent	In this case also it was held that rights under Article 30(1) are subject to reasonable restrictions.
Precedent	52.
Precedent	The case of <CITAT ION_1596466> reported in (1971) Supp.
Precedent	SCR 677 does not deal with Article 29(2) and its effect on Article 30.
Precedent	In this case Punjabi was made the sole medium of instruction and examination under <ORG> Act.
Precedent	It was held that this violated the rights under Article 29(1) as well as Article 30(1) inasmuch as the right to have an educational institution of a choice includes the right to have a choice of the medium of instruction also.
Precedent	53.
Precedent	In the second case of <CITATION_1596466> reported in (1971) Supp.
Precedent	SCR 688 <ORG> was formed to perpetuate the memory of the founder of <ORG>.
Precedent	It ran various institutions in the country.
Precedent	The collages managed and administered by the <ORG> were, before the Punjab Reorganisation Act , affiliated to <ORG>.
Precedent	After the reorganisation of the State of Punjab in 1969, <ORG> passed the Guru Nank University (Amritsar) Act .
Precedent	Colleges in the districts specified ceased to be affiliated to <ORG>  and were to be associated with and admitted to the privileges of the new university.
Precedent	Sub-section (2) of Section 4 of the Act provided that the university "shall make provision for study and research on the life and teaching of <NAME> and their cultural and religious impact in the context of Indian and World Civilisation; and Sub-section (3) enjoined the <ORG> "to promote studies to provide for research in Punjabi language and literature and to undertake measures for the development of Punjabi language, literature and culture".
Precedent	By Clause 2(1)(a) of the Statutes framed under the Act, the colleges were required to have a regularly constituted governing body consisting of not more than 20 persons approved by the <ORG> including, among others, two representatives of the <ORG> and the principal of the <ORG>.
Precedent	Under Clause (1)(3) if these requirements were not complied with the affiliation was liable to be withdrawn.
Precedent	By Clause 18 the staff initially appointed were to be approved by the Vice Chancell or and subsequent changes had to be reported to the <ORG> for the Vice- Chancellor's approval.
Precedent	And by Clause 18 non- government colleges were to comply with the requirements laid down in the ordinance governing service and conduct of teachers.
Precedent	It was held that Clause 2(1)(a) interfered with the right of the religious minority to administer their educational institutions, but that Clause 18 did not suffer from the same vice.
Precedent	It was held that ordinances prescribing regulations governing the conditions of service and conduct of teachers must be considered to be one enacted in the larger interest of the institution to ensure their efficiency and excellence.
Precedent	It was similarly held that Sub- sections (2) and (3) of Section 4 do not offend any of the rights under Articles 29(1) and 30(1).
Precedent	It must be observed that, whilst dealing with the Articles 29 and 30, this <ORG> observed as follows: "It will be observed that Article 29(1) is wider than Article 30(1 ), in that, while any Section of the citizens including th e minorities, can invoke the rights guaranteed under Article 29(1 ), the rights guaranteed under Article 30(1) are only available to the minorities based on religion or language.
Precedent	It is not necessary for Article 30(1) that the minority should be both a religious minority as well as linguistic minority.
Precedent	It is sufficient if it is one or the other or both.
Precedent	A reading of these two Articles together would lead us to conclude that a religious or linguistic minority has a right to establish and administer educational institutions of its choice for effectively conserving its distinctive language, script or culture, which right however is subject to the regulatory power of the <ORG> for maintaining and facilitating the excellence of its standards.
Precedent	This right is further subject to Clause (2) of Article 29 which provides that no citizen shall be denied admission into any educational institution which is maintained by the <ORG> or receives aid out of <ORG> funds, on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of  them."
Precedent	(emphasis supplied)  54.
Precedent	Thus, even in 1971, this Court has held that Article 29(2) governs Article 30(1).
Precedent	The law laid down in <NAME> case, in <ORG> case and in Kerala Education Bill's case has been reaffirmed.
Precedent	Till this date no contrary view has been taken.
Precedent	Not a single case has held that rights under Article 30(1) would not be governed by Article 29(2).
Precedent	55.
Precedent	The authority on which strong reliance has been placed by the counsel of the minority is <ORG> case (supra).
Precedent	<ORG> was affiliated to <ORG>.
Precedent	A resolution was passe by the Senate of the <ORG> that all instruction, teaching and training in courses of studies in respect of which the <ORG> was competent to hold examinations shall be conducted by the university and shall be imported by teachers of the <ORG>.
Precedent	Section 5 of the Act provided that no educational institution situated within the <ORG> shall, save with the sanction of <ORG> , be associated in any way with or seek admission to any privilege of any other <ORG> established by law.
Statute	Section 33A(1)(a) of the Act provided that every <ORG> other than a <ORG> <ORG> or a <ORG> maintained by the <ORG>, shall be under the management of a governing body which included among others, the Principal of the <ORG> and a representative of the <ORG> nominated by the Vice-Chancellor.
Statute	Section 33A(1)(b)(I) provided that in the case of recruitment of the Principal, a selection committee is required to be constituted consisting of, among others, a representatives of the <ORG> nominated by the Vice-Chancellor and (ii) in the case of selection of a member of the teaching staff of the <ORG> a selection committee consisting of the Principal and a representative of the university nominated by the Vice-Chancellor.
Statute	Sub-section (3) of the Section stated that the provisions of Sub-section (1) of Section 33A shall be deemed to be a condition of affiliation of every college referr ed to in that sub-section.
Statute	Section 39 provided that within the <ORG> area all post-graduate instruction, teaching and training shall be conducted by the <ORG> or by such affiliated <ORG> or institution and in such subjects as may be prescribed by statutes.
Statute	Section 40(1) enacted that the Court of the <ORG> may determine that all instructions, teaching and training in courses of studies in respect of which the <ORG> is competent to hold examinations shall be conducted by the <ORG> and shall be imparted by the teachers of the <ORG>.
Statute	Sub-section (2) of Section 40 stated that <ORG> shall issue a notification declaring that the provisions of Section 41 shall come into force on such date as may be specified in the notification.
Statute	Section 41(1) of the Act stated that all colleges within the <ORG> area which are admitted to the privilege of the university under Section 5(3) and all colleges within the said area which may hereafter be affiliated to the <ORG> shall  be constituent colleges of the <ORG>.
Statute	Sub-section (4) stated that the relations of the constituent colleges and other institutions within the <ORG> area shall be governed by statutes to be made in that behalf.
Statute	Section 51A(a)(b) enacted that no member of the teaching other academic and non-teaching staff of an affiliated college shall be dismissed or removed or reduced in rank except after an enquiry in accordance with the procedure prescribed in Clause (a) and the penalty to be inflicted on him is approved by the Vice-Chancellor or any other Officer of the <ORG> authorised by the Vice-Chancellor in this behalf.
Statute	Similarly Clause (b) of Sub-section (2) required that such termination should be approved by the Vice-Chancellor or any officer of the <ORG> authorised by the Vice-Chancellor in this behalf.
Statute	Section 52A(1) enacted that any dispute between the governing body and any member of the teaching and other staff shall, on a request of the governing body or of the member concerned be referred  to a tribunal of arbitration consisting of one member nominated by the governing body of the college, one member nominated by the member concerned and an umpire appointed by the Vice-Chancellor.
Argument	<ORG> contended that they had a fundamental right to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice and that such a right included the right of affiliation.
Argument	They therefore challenged the constitutional validity of the above Sections.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is in this context that various observations have been made.
RatioOfTheDecision	These observations cannot be drawn out of context.
RatioOfTheDecision	In this case it was an admitted position, as set out by Justice <NAME>, that children of all classes and creeds were admitted to the college provided they met the qualifying standards.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus the <ORG> never claimed the right to only admit students of its own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	It acknowledged the fact that it had to admit students of all classes and creeds.
RatioOfTheDecision	The majority Judgment, therefore, did not deal with the question or interplay between Arti cles 29(2) and 30.
RatioOfTheDecision	Even though it did not deal with the interplay of Articles 29(2) and 30, it was clear that reasoning of the majority is based on the fact that the <ORG> did not deny admissions to the students of other communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	This is clearly indicated by the test which had been laid down by the majority.
RatioOfTheDecision	This test reads as follows:  "Such regulation must satisfy a dual test - the test of reasonableness, and the test that it is regulative of the educational character of the institution and is conducive to making the institution an effective vehicle of education for the minority community or other persons who resort to it."
RatioOfTheDecision	(emphasis supplied) Thus it is held by the majority that the institute is to be made an effective vehicle of education not just for the minority community but also for other persons who resort to do.
RatioOfTheDecision	This indicates that the majority made the observations on the understanding that admissions were not restricted only to students of minority community once <ORG> aid was received.
RatioOfTheDecision	This  aspect is clearly brought out in the Judgment of Justice <NAME> who, whilst dealing with the various provisions of the Constitution, held as follows:  "A glance at the context and scheme of Part III of the Constitution would show that the Constitution makers did not intend to confer absolute rights on a religious or linguistic minority to establish and administer educational institutions.
RatioOfTheDecision	The associate Article 29(2) imposes one restriction on the right in Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	No religious or linguistic minority establishing and administering an educational institution which receives aid from the <ORG> funds shall deny admission to any citizen to the institution on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right to admit a student to an educational institution is admittedly comprised in the right to administer it.
RatioOfTheDecision	This right is partly curtailed by Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	The right of admission is further curtailed by Article 15(4) which provides an exception to Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 15(4) enab les the <ORG> to make any special provision for the advancement of any socially and educationally backward class of citizens or for the scheduled caste and scheduled tribes in the matter of admission in the educational institutions maintained by the <ORG> or receiving aid from the <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 28(3) imposes a third restriction on the right in Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	It provides that no person attending any educational institution recognised or receiving aid by the <ORG> shall be required to take part in any religious instruction that may be imparted in such institution or to attend any religious worship that may be conducted in such institution or in any premises attached thereto unless such person or, if such person is a minor, his guardian has given his consent thereto.
RatioOfTheDecision	Obviously, Article 28(3) prohibits a religious minority establishing and administering an educational institution which receives aid or is recognised by the <ORG> from compelling any citizen reading in the institution to receive religious instruct ion against his wishes or if minor against the wishes of his guardian.
RatioOfTheDecision	It cannot be disputed that the right of a religious minority to impart religious instruction in an educational institution forms part of the right to administer the institution.
RatioOfTheDecision	And yet Article 28(3) curtails that right to a certain extent.
RatioOfTheDecision	To sum up Articles 29(2), 15(4) and 28(3) place certain express limitations on the right in Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	There are also certain implied limitations on this right.
Precedent	The right should be read subject to those implied limitations."
Precedent	(emphasis supplied) Thus even in this authority the principle that Article 29(2) applies to Article 30(1) has been recognised and upheld.
Precedent	This case also holds that reasonable restrictions can be placed on the rights under Article 30(1) subject to the test set out hereinabove.
Precedent	56.
Precedent	In the case of <CITATION_1993702> reported in (1975) 3 SCR 810 the minority college was affiliated to <ORG>.
Precedent	It applies for permission to start teaching in certain courses of study.
Precedent	T he <ORG>, as a condition of permitting the additional subjects, insisted that <ORG> must be re-constituted in line with Statute 14-A which provided that the principal of the <ORG> and senior-most staff member should be part of <ORG>.
Precedent	The Petitioners filed a Writ Petition in <ORG> challenging the imposition of such a condition on the ground that it was violative of their rights under Article 30(1).
Precedent	<ORG> dismissed the Writ Petition.
Precedent	Therefore the Petitioners came to this Court.
Precedent	The majority of Judges upheld the order of <ORG>, inter alia, on the ground that the right under Article 30(1) is not the absolute right and that it is a right which can be restricted.
Precedent	After considering the various authorities (including some of those set out hereinabove) it was held that reasonable regulations are desirable, necessary and constitutional, provided they shape but not cut out of shape the individual personality of the minority.
Precedent	It was held as follows:  "I n all these cases administrative autonomy is imperilled transgressing purely regulatory limits.
RatioOfTheDecision	In our case autonomy is virtually left intact and refurbishing, not restructuring, is prescribed.
RatioOfTheDecision	The core of the right is not gouged out at all and the regulation is at once reasonable and calculated to promote excellence of the institution - a text book instance of constitutional conditions."
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus a condition that <ORG> be reconstituted is upheld.
RatioOfTheDecision	To be noted that the directly affects the right of administration.
RatioOfTheDecision	Now compulsory the principal and one of the staff members would be part of <ORG>.
RatioOfTheDecision	Yet it has been held that this is not violative of rights under Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	57.
RatioOfTheDecision	In the case of <ORG> <CITATION_13862901> , one of the questions was the applicability of Article 29(2) to Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	Even in this case it has been accepted that Article 29(2) applies to Section 30(1) .
RatioOfTheDecision	However, the majority of the Judges, after noting that Article 29(2) applies to Article 30(1  ), sought to compromise and/or strike a balance between Articles 29(2) and 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	They therefore prescribed a ratio of 50% to be admitted on merits and 50% to be admitted by the <ORG> from their own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	All Counsel, whether appearing for the minorities or for the <ORG>s/local authorities attacked this judgment and submitted that it is not correct.
RatioOfTheDecision	Of course Counsel for the minorities were claiming a right to admit students of their own community even to the extent of 100%.
RatioOfTheDecision	On the other hand the submission was that once <ORG> aid is taken Article 29(2) applied and not even a single student could be admitted on basis of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus all counsel attacked the judgment as being not correct.
RatioOfTheDecision	In matters of interpretation, there can be no compromise.
RatioOfTheDecision	As stated above if the language and meaning are clear then Courts must give effect to it irrespective of the consequence.
RatioOfTheDecision	With the greatest of respect to the learned Judges concerned, once it was held that Article 29(2) ap plied to Article 30 , there was no question of trying to balance rights or to seek a compromise.
RatioOfTheDecision	58.
RatioOfTheDecision	Justice <NAME> dissented from the majority view.
RatioOfTheDecision	It must be noted that in <NAME> case, in his minority judgment, he has held that Article 29(2) governs Article 30(1) and that if the minority educational institute chooses to take aid it must comply with the constitutional mandate of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	The Judgment in St. Stephens case is of recent origin.
RatioOfTheDecision	It therefore cannot form the basis for applying the principles of "State Decisis".
RatioOfTheDecision	59.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus, from any point of view i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	historical or contextual or on principles of pure interpretation or on principles of "stare decisis" the only interpretation possible is that the rights under Article 30(1) are conferred on minorities to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice at their own cost.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right is a special right which is given by way of protection so that the majority, which is politically powerful, does not prevent the minorities  from establishing their educational institutions.
RatioOfTheDecision	This right was not created because the minorities were economically and socially backward or that their children would not be able to compete on merit with children of other communities.
RatioOfTheDecision	This right was not conferred in order to create a special category of the citizens.
RatioOfTheDecision	What has been granted to them is a right which was equal to the rights enjoyed by the majority community, namely, to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice at their own cost.
RatioOfTheDecision	As the institution was to be established and maintained at their own expense no right to receive aid has been conferred on the minority institute.
RatioOfTheDecision	All that Article 30(2) provides is that the <ORG> while granting aid would not discriminate merely on the ground that an educational institute was under the management of a minority.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 30(2) has been so worded as the framers were aware that once <ORG> aid was taken some aspects of the right of administration would have to be compromised and give n up.
RatioOfTheDecision	The minority educational institute have a choice.
RatioOfTheDecision	They need not take <ORG> aid.
RatioOfTheDecision	But if they choose to take <ORG> aid then they have to comply with constitutional mandates which are based on principles which are as important as if not more important than the rights given to the minorities.
RatioOfTheDecision	Our Constitution mandates that the <ORG> cannot discriminate on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Our Constitution mandates that all citizens are equal and that no citizen can be denied admission into educational institution maintained by the <ORG> or receiving aid out of <ORG> funds on grounds only of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus if <ORG> aid is taken the minority educational institution must then not refuse admission to students of other communities on any of those grounds.
RatioOfTheDecision	In other words, they cannot then insist that they would admit students only of their community.
RatioOfTheDecision	Of course, as stated above, preferences could always be given to students of their own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	But preference necessarily implies that all other things are equal, i.e.
RatioOfTheDecision	that on merit the student of their community is equal to the merit of the student of other community.
RatioOfTheDecision	As stated above, in para 37, in schools the minority community would have a larger amount of leeway and so long as the school admits a sufficient number of outsiders Article 29(2) would not be violated if the refusal is not made on the basis of the religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Of course, at the under-graduate and post-graduate stages merit would have to be the criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	At these stages there are common entrance examinations by which inter se merit can be assessed.
RatioOfTheDecision	But even here, the minority educational institute can admit students of its own community on grounds like those set out in para 37 above.
RatioOfTheDecision	They could give some preference to students coming from their own schools.
RatioOfTheDecision	There could be interviews wherein not more than 15% marks can be allotted.
RatioOfTheDecision	Students of their community will be able to compete on merit also.
RatioOfTheDecision	All t hese would ensure that a sufficient number of students of their own community receive admissions.
RatioOfTheDecision	But the minority institute, once it receives <ORG> aid, cannot refuse to abide by the constitutional mandate of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	It would be paradoxical to unsettle settled law at such a late stage.
RatioOfTheDecision	It would be paradoxical to hold that the rights under Article 30(1) are subject to municipal and other laws, but that they are not subject to the constitutional mandate under Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	It would be paradoxical to held that Article 30(1) is subject to Article 28(3) but not to Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	It must be remembered that when Article 29(2) was introduced it was part of the same Article (viz.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 23 ) which also included what is now Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	Not only <ORG> but also the fact that they were part of the same Article shows that Article 29(2) was intended by the framers of the Constitution to apply even to institutions established under Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus Article 29(2) governs educational  institutions established under Article 30(1).
RatioOfTheDecision	The language is clear and unambiguous.
RatioOfTheDecision	It is clear that Article 30(1) has full play so long as the educational institution is established and maintained and administered by the minority at their own costs.
RatioOfTheDecision	Article 30(2) purposely and significantly does not make taking or granting of aid compulsory.
RatioOfTheDecision	The minority educational institution need not take aid.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, it is chooses to take aid then it can hardly claim that it would not abide by the Constitutional mandate of Article 29(2).
RatioOfTheDecision	Once the language is clear and unambiguous full effect must be given to Article 29(2) irrespective of the consequences.
RatioOfTheDecision	This can be the only interpretation.
RatioOfTheDecision	The only interplay between Articles 29(2) and 30(1) is that once <ORG> aid is taken, then students of all communities must be admitted.
RatioOfTheDecision	In others words, no citizen can be refused admission on grounds of religion, race, caste or creed or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	Reserving seats for students of one's own community would in effect be refusing ad mission on grounds of religion, race, caste, or creed.
RatioOfTheDecision	As there is no conflict the question of balancing rights under Article 30(1) and Article 29(2) of the Constitution does not arise.
RatioOfTheDecision	As stated by <ORG> in the case of <ORG> v. <NAME> (411 US 1), it is not the province of this Court to create substantive Constitutional rights in the name of guaranteeing equal protection.
RatioOfTheDecision	60.
RatioOfTheDecision	In view of above discussion we answer the questions as follows: Q.1.
RatioOfTheDecision	What is the meaning and content of the expression "minorities" in Article 30 of the Constitution of India?
RatioOfTheDecision	A. Linguistic and religious minorities are covered by the expression "minority" under Article 30 of the Constitution.
RatioOfTheDecision	Since reorganization of the States in India has been on linguistic lines, therefore, for the purpose of determining the minority, the unit will be the State and not the whole of India.
RatioOfTheDecision	Thus, religious and linguistic minorities, who have been put at par in Article 30 , have to be consi dered state wise.
RatioOfTheDecision	Q.2.
RatioOfTheDecision	What is meant by the expression "religion" in Article 30(1)?
Precedent	Can the followers of a sect or denomination of a particular religion claim protection under Article 30(1) on the basis that they constitute a minority in the State, even though the followers of that religion are in majority in that State?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	This question need not be answered by this <ORG>; it will be dealt with by a regular <ORG>.
Precedent	Q.3(a) What are the indicia for treating an educational institution as a minority educational institution?
Precedent	Would an institution be regarded as a minority educational institution because it was established by a person(s) belonging to a religious or linguistic minority or its being administered by a person(s) belonging to a religious or linguistic minority?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	This question need not be answered by this <ORG>, it will be dealt with by a regular <ORG>.
Precedent	Q.3(b) To what extent can professional education be treated as a matter coming under minorities rights under Article 30?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	Article 30(1) gives reli gious and linguistic minorities the right to establish and administer educational institutions of their choice.
Precedent	The use of the words "of their choice", indicates that professional educational institutions would be covered by Article 30.
Precedent	Q.4.
Precedent	Whether the admission of students to minority educational institution, whether aided or unaided, can be regulated by <ORG> or by the <ORG> to which the institution is affiliated?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	Admission of students to unaided minority educational institutions, viz., Schools where scope for merit based selection is practically nil, cannot be regulated by the <ORG> or the <ORG> (except for providing the qualifications and minimum conditions of eligibility in the interest of academic standards).
RatioOfTheDecision	Right to admit students being an essential facet of right to administer educational institutions of their choice, as contemplated under Article 30 of the Constitution, <ORG> or the <ORG> may not be entitled to interfere with that right in respect  of unaided minority institutions provided however that the admission to the unaided educational institutions is on transparent basis and the merit is the criteria.
RatioOfTheDecision	The right to administer, not being an absolute one, there could be regulator measures for ensuring educational standards and maintain exceptance thereof and it is more so, in the matter of admission to undergraduate Colleges and professional institutions.
RatioOfTheDecision	The moment aid is received or taken by a minority educational institution it would be governed by Article 29(2) and would then not be able to refuse admission on grounds of religion, race, caste, language or any of them.
RatioOfTheDecision	In other words it cannot then give preference to students of its own community.
RatioOfTheDecision	Observance of inter se merit amongst the applicants must be ensured.
Precedent	In the case of aided professional institutions, it can also be stipulated that passing of common entrance test held by the <ORG> agency is necessary to seek admission.
Precedent	Q.5(a) Whether the minority's rights to establish and administer  educational institutions of their choice will include the procedure and method of admission and selection of students?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	A minority institution may have its own procedure and method of admission as well as selection of students, but such procedure must be fair and transparent and selection of students in professional and higher educational colleges should be on the basis of merit.
Precedent	The procedure adopted or selection made should not tantamount to mal-administration.
Precedent	Even an unaided minority institution, ought not to ignore merit of the students for admission, while exercising its right to admit students to the colleges, aforesaid, as in that event.
Precedent	The institution will fail to achieve excellence.
Precedent	Q.5(b) Whether the minority institutions' right of admission of students and to lay down procedure and method of admission, if any, would be affected in any way by the receipt of <ORG> aid?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	Further to what is stated in answer to question No.
Precedent	4, it must be stated that whilst giving aid to professional institutio ns, it would be permissible for the authority giving aid to prescribe by-rules or regulations, the conditions on the basis of which admission will be granted to different aided colleges by virtue of merit, coupled with the reservation policy of the state.
Precedent	The merit may be determined either through a common entrance test conducted by the <ORG> or the <ORG> followed by counselling, or on the basis of an entrance test conducted by individual institutions - the method to be followed is for the university or the government to decide.
Precedent	The authority may also devise other means to ensure that admission is granted to an aided professional institution on the basis of merit.
Precedent	In the case of such institutions, it will be permissible for the government or the university to provide that consideration should be shown to the weaker sections of the society.
Precedent	Q.5(c) Whether the statutory Provisions which regulate the facets of administration like control over educational agencies, control over governing bodies, conditi ons of affiliation including recognition/withdrawal thereof, and appointment of state employees, teachers and Principals including their service conditions and regulation of fees, etc.
Precedent	would interfere with the right of administration of minorities?
Precedent	A.
RatioOfTheDecision	So far as the statutory provisions regulating the facets administration is concerned, in case of an unaided minority educational institution, the regulatory measure of control should be minimal and the conditions of recognition as well as conditions of affiliation to an <ORG> or Board have to be complied with, but in the matter of day-to-day <ORG>, like appointment of staff, teaching and non-teaching and administrative control over them, the <ORG> should have the freedom and there should not be any external controlling agency.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, a rational procedure for selection of teaching staff and for taking disciplinary action has to be evolved by the <ORG> itself.
RatioOfTheDecision	For redressing the grievances of such employees who are subjected to punishment or  termination from service, a mechanism will have to be evolved and in our opinion, appropriate tribunals could be constituted, and till then, such tribunal could be presided over by a Judicial officer of the rank of District Judge.
RatioOfTheDecision	The state or other controlling authorities, however, can always prescribe the minimum qualifications, salaries, experience and other conditions bearing on the merit of an individual for being appointed as a teacher of an educational institution.
RatioOfTheDecision	Regulations can be framed governing service conditions for teaching and other staff for whom aid is provided by the <ORG> without interfering with overall administrative control of Management over the staff, <ORG> representative can be associated with the selection committee and the guidelines for selection can be laid down.
RatioOfTheDecision	In regard to un-aided minority educational institutions such regulations, which will ensure a check over unfair practices and general welfare, of teachers could be framed.
RatioOfTheDecision	There could be appropriate me chanism to ensure that no capitation fee is charged and profiteering is not restored to.
RatioOfTheDecision	The extent of regulations will not be the same for aided and un-aided institutions.
Precedent	Q.6(a) Where can minority institution be operationally located?
Precedent	Where a religious or linguistic minority in State 'A' establishes an educational institution in the said State, can such educational institution grant preferential admission/reservations and other benefits to members of the religious/linguistic group from other States where they are non-minorities?
Precedent	A.

Precedent	Q.7.
Precedent	Whether the member of a linguistic non-minority in one State can establish a trust/society in another State a nd claim minority status in that State?

Precedent	Q.8 Whether the ratio laid down by this <ORG> in the <ORG> case (<ORG> <CITATION_13862901> is correct?
Precedent	If no, what order?
Precedent	A.
RatioOfTheDecision	The ratio laid down in <ORG> College case is not correct.
RatioOfTheDecision	Once State aid is taken and Article 29(2) comes into play, then no question arises of trying to balance Article 29(2) and 31.
Precedent	Article 29(2) must be given its full effect.
Precedent	Q.9 Whether the decisions of this <ORG> in <CITATION_1775396> .
Precedent	(except where it holds that primary education is a fundamental right) and the scheme framed thereunder require reconsideration/modification and if yes, what?
Precedent	A.
RatioOfTheDecision	The scheme framed by this <ORG> in <NAME> case and the direction to impose the same, except where it holds that primary education is a fundamental right, is unconstitutional.
RatioOfTheDecision	However, the principle that there should not be capitation fee or profiteering is correct.
RatioOfTheDecision	<NAME> nable surplus to meet cost of expansion and augmentation of facilities does not, however, amount to profiteering.
Precedent	Q.10 Whether the non-minorities have the right to establish and administer educational institution under Articles 21 and 29(1) read with Article 14 and 15(1 ), in the same manner and to the same extent as minority institutions?
Precedent	and Q.11 What is the meaning of the expressions "Education" and "Educational Institutions" in various provisions of the Constitution?
Precedent	Is the right to establish and administer educational institutions guaranteed under the Constitution?
Precedent	A.
Precedent	The expression "education" in the Articles of the Constitution means and includes education at all levels from the primary school level up to the post-graduate level.
Precedent	It includes professional education.
Precedent	The expression "educational institutions" means institutions that impart education, where "education" is as understood hereinabove.
Precedent	The right to establish and administer educational institutions is guaranteed under the Constitution to all  citizens under Article 19(1)(g) and 26 , and to minorities specifically under Article 30.
Precedent	All citizens have a right to establish and administer educational institutions under Articles 19(1)(g) and 26, but this right will be subject to the provisions of Articles 19(6) and 26(a).
Precedent	However, minority institutions will have a right to admit students belonging to the minority group, in the manner as discussed in this judgment.
